The Historical Defense of Uthman and Abu Dharr
Nasafi refutes Uthman's alleged banishment of Abu Dharr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi refutes the claim that Uthman banished Abu Dharr through historical reports and logical justifications.

Core Idea
Uthman's treatment of Abu Dharr was justified and not a banishment.

This lesson examines the accusation that Uthman banished Abu Dharr. Nasafi presents several counter-narratives, including a denial from Hasan al-Basri and a report that Abu Dharr himself chose to leave. The goal is to see how early Muslim scholars defended the Companions' actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice how Nasafi builds his defense in layers.
2
Identify the three arguments
The passage contains three distinct defenses: the report from Hasan al-Basri, the justification based on public benefit, and the story of Abu Dharr's voluntary departure. Identify each one.
These are not all of equal strength; note how Nasafi uses them cumulatively.
3
Consider the underlying principle
Ask yourself what assumption Nasafi makes about the caliph's authority. He sees nothing wrong with sending a resident away for a perceived benefit. This reflects a view of leadership discretion.
This connects to broader discussions of political authority in Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما يزعمون أنه نفى أبا ذر ليس بثابت أيضا، وروى أن الحسن البصري كان جالسًا في مجلسه فدخل عليه رجل فقال: أعثمان أخرج أبا ذر؟ فقال الحسن : لا . كذبوا . فتعجب أصحابه من ذلك وقالوا له: ما معنى ما دار بينكما من الكلام؟ فقال: إنه سأل على طريق التصحيف أعثمان أخرج أبا ذر؟ فقلت: لا، ولو ثبت لكان من الجائز أنه أخرجه لمصلحة رآها في ذلك. وروى أن أبا ذر كان رجلاً متزهدًا، وكان عثمان موسرا وكان يعيش عيش الأغنياء، وكان أبو ذر يطلب منه أن يقتدي بأبي بكر وعمر - رضي الله عنهما - في رفض الزينة ومجانبة الشبهات وكان يخاشنه في الكلام في ذلك المعنى على وجه كان يذهب بهيبة الخلافة، فرأى المصلحة في أن بعثه إلى الربذة، ولا عيب في هذا، وروي أن معاوية كتب إلى عثمان يشكو أبا ذر فكتب عثمان إلى أبي ذر يستقدمه إلى المدينة، فأبى أبو ذر، وقال: سمعت رسول الله عليه السلام يقول: "إذا بلغت عمارة المدينة إلى موضع كذا فاخرج عنها" وقد بلغت العمارة ذلك الموضع فخيره عثمان أي البلاد أحب إليه؟ فاختار الربذة، فقال له: فاخرج إليها، ولو لم يرو شيء من هذه الوجوه لكان الواجب حمل أمر عثمان مع زهده وورعه وجلال قدره في الدين في كونه من الذين هاجروا هجرتين، وختنا لرسول الله على الابنتين وإنفاقه في نصرة الدين وتجهيز جيش المسلمين كل نفيس وخطير من الأموال ومضنون به من النعم، وكونه من المبشرين بالجنة، وقول النبي عليه السلام فيه عثمان "أخي ورفيقي في الجنة" وقوله عليه السلام - لما ستر ركبته عند مجيء عثمان -: "ألا أستحي ممن تستحي منه ملائكة السماء"، وقوله عليه السلام فيه وفي علي رضي الله عنهما لما أتياه في شيء: "هكذا تدخلان الجنة لا يحبكما إلا مؤمن ولا يبغضكما إلا منافق" وروي أنه عليه السلام قال ...
And what they claim that he banished Abu Dharr is also not established. And it is narrated that al-Hasan al-Basri was sitting in his gathering when a man entered and said: Did Uthman expel Abu Dharr? Al-Hasan said: No. They lied. His companions were astonished and said to him: What is the meaning of the conversation between you? He said: He asked in a distorted manner: Did Uthman expel Abu Dharr? I said: No. And if it were established, it would be possible that he expelled him for a benefit he saw in that. And it is narrated that Abu Dharr was a man of asceticism, and Uthman was wealthy and lived the life of the rich, and Abu Dharr would ask him to emulate Abu Bakr and Umar in rejecting adornment and avoiding ambiguities, and he would speak harshly to him in that matter in a way that diminished the awe of the caliphate. So he saw the benefit in sending him to al-Rabada, and there is no fault in this. And it is narrated that Muawiya wrote to Uthman complaining about Abu Dharr, so Uthman wrote to Abu Dharr summoning him to Madina, but Abu Dharr refused and said: I heard the Messenger of God say: 'When the building of Madina reaches such and such a place, then leave it.' And the building had reached that place. So Uthman gave him the choice of whichever land he preferred, and he chose al-Rabada, so he said to him: Go out to it. And even if none of these reports were narrated, it would be necessary to judge Uthman's affair, given his asceticism, piety, high standing in religion, being one of the two migrations, the son-in-law of the Messenger of God for two daughters, spending noble and valuable wealth in supporting the religion and equipping the Muslim army, being among those given glad tidings of Paradise, and the Prophet's saying about Uthman: 'He is my brother and companion in Paradise', and his saying when he covered his knee at Uthman's coming: 'Should I not feel shy of one whom the angels of heaven feel shy of?' and his saying about him and Ali when they came to him for something: 'Thus you will enter Paradise; none loves you except a believer and none hates you except a hypocrite.' And it is narrated that he said...
Source pages p. 1161

Commentary
This passage defends Uthman against the accusation that he banished Abu Dharr. It has three parts: First, it questions the historical reliability of the claim, citing al-Hasan al-Basri's denial and explanation of a possible misinterpretation. Second, it provides a reasonable justification: Uthman was wealthy and Abu Dharr, being ascetic, was critical of Uthman's lifestyle, and Uthman thought it beneficial to send him to al-Rabada to preserve the dignity of the caliphate. Third, it presents an alternative narrative from Abu Dharr himself that he left voluntarily due to a prophecy. Finally, Nasafi lays down a principle: even without these external reports, Uthman's outstanding merits—his piety, his having made two migrations, being a husband of two of the Prophet's daughters, his generous spending for Islam, being promised Paradise, and the Prophet's praise for him and Ali—oblige us to interpret his actions favorably. This establishes a precedent for defending the Companions' actions by their high moral status.

Key Terms
نفى أبا ذر
الحسن البصري
الربذة
المصلحة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Uthman unjustly banished Abu Dharr as a punishment.
Correction: Nasafi shows the claim is not established, and even if it were, it could be justified by public benefit or Abu Dharr's own choice.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did Abu Dharr claim the Prophet told him about leaving Madina?
A) To go to al-Rabada
B) To leave when the building reaches a certain point
C) To go to Syria
D) To stay with Uthman

Key Takeaway
The accusation that Uthman banished Abu Dharr is historically weak and can be reasonably explained away.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear an accusation against a person of authority, do you immediately accept it or do you seek to understand the full context? What stops you from jumping to conclusions? Commit to investigating at least one controversial claim about a historical figure this week with the same care shown here.
?
This lesson shows that even a respected companion like Abu Dharr could be sent away for the greater good. Is there a situation in your life where you need to accept a difficult decision for the benefit of others, even if it feels unjust? What would it take for you to submit to that wisdom?
?
Abu Dharr's asceticism and Uthman's wealth created tension. How do you handle differences in lifestyle or piety within your community? Do you let them divide you, or can you see the wisdom in different approaches? Name one step you will take this week to build unity despite differences.

The Principle of Judging Companions by Their Virtues
Nasafi argues for judging Uthman's actions by his virtues.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the principle that a Companion's established virtues should lead us to interpret his actions positively.

Core Idea
Uthman's high status obliges us to judge his actions favorably.

Nasafi now argues that even without the specific reports, Uthman's impeccable character and the Prophet's praise for him demand that we give him the benefit of the doubt. This lesson explores the logic of this principle and the list of Uthman's virtues that support it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice that this is a conditional statement: 'even if none of these reports were narrated, it would be necessary...'
The phrase 'ولو لم يرو' signals a shift to a more fundamental principle.
2
Identify the virtues listed
The passage enumerates several of Uthman's virtues: his asceticism, piety, double migration, being a son-in-law of the Prophet, spending for Islam, being promised Paradise, and specific hadiths praising him. List them.
These are not just random facts; each is a reason to trust Uthman's judgment.
3
Understand the underlying principle
Nasafi is arguing that the high moral and religious standing of a Companion obliges us to interpret ambiguous actions in the best possible way. This is a key principle in Sunni theology for defending the Companions.
This principle is often invoked in discussions of the 'Adl of the Sahaba.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما يزعمون أنه نفى أبا ذر ليس بثابت أيضا، وروى أن الحسن البصري كان جالسًا في مجلسه فدخل عليه رجل فقال: أعثمان أخرج أبا ذر؟ فقال الحسن : لا . كذبوا . فتعجب أصحابه من ذلك وقالوا له: ما معنى ما دار بينكما من الكلام؟ فقال: إنه سأل على طريق التصحيف أعثمان أخرج أبا ذر؟ فقلت: لا، ولو ثبت لكان من الجائز أنه أخرجه لمصلحة رآها في ذلك. وروى أن أبا ذر كان رجلاً متزهدًا، وكان عثمان موسرا وكان يعيش عيش الأغنياء، وكان أبو ذر يطلب منه أن يقتدي بأبي بكر وعمر - رضي الله عنهما - في رفض الزينة ومجانبة الشبهات وكان يخاشنه في الكلام في ذلك المعنى على وجه كان يذهب بهيبة الخلافة، فرأى المصلحة في أن بعثه إلى الربذة، ولا عيب في هذا، وروي أن معاوية كتب إلى عثمان يشكو أبا ذر فكتب عثمان إلى أبي ذر يستقدمه إلى المدينة، فأبى أبو ذر، وقال: سمعت رسول الله عليه السلام يقول: "إذا بلغت عمارة المدينة إلى موضع كذا فاخرج عنها" وقد بلغت العمارة ذلك الموضع فخيره عثمان أي البلاد أحب إليه؟ فاختار الربذة، فقال له: فاخرج إليها، ولو لم يرو شيء من هذه الوجوه لكان الواجب حمل أمر عثمان مع زهده وورعه وجلال قدره في الدين في كونه من الذين هاجروا هجرتين، وختنا لرسول الله على الابنتين وإنفاقه في نصرة الدين وتجهيز جيش المسلمين كل نفيس وخطير من الأموال ومضنون به من النعم، وكونه من المبشرين بالجنة، وقول النبي عليه السلام فيه عثمان "أخي ورفيقي في الجنة" وقوله عليه السلام - لما ستر ركبته عند مجيء عثمان -: "ألا أستحي ممن تستحي منه ملائكة السماء"، وقوله عليه السلام فيه وفي علي رضي الله عنهما لما أتياه في شيء: "هكذا تدخلان الجنة لا يحبكما إلا مؤمن ولا يبغضكما إلا منافق" وروي أنه عليه السلام قال ...
And what they claim that he banished Abu Dharr is also not established. And it is narrated that al-Hasan al-Basri was sitting in his gathering when a man entered and said: Did Uthman expel Abu Dharr? Al-Hasan said: No. They lied. His companions were astonished and said to him: What is the meaning of the conversation between you? He said: He asked in a distorted manner: Did Uthman expel Abu Dharr? I said: No. And if it were established, it would be possible that he expelled him for a benefit he saw in that. And it is narrated that Abu Dharr was a man of asceticism, and Uthman was wealthy and lived the life of the rich, and Abu Dharr would ask him to emulate Abu Bakr and Umar in rejecting adornment and avoiding ambiguities, and he would speak harshly to him in that matter in a way that diminished the awe of the caliphate. So he saw the benefit in sending him to al-Rabada, and there is no fault in this. And it is narrated that Muawiya wrote to Uthman complaining about Abu Dharr, so Uthman wrote to Abu Dharr summoning him to Madina, but Abu Dharr refused and said: I heard the Messenger of God say: 'When the building of Madina reaches such and such a place, then leave it.' And the building had reached that place. So Uthman gave him the choice of whichever land he preferred, and he chose al-Rabada, so he said to him: Go out to it. And even if none of these reports were narrated, it would be necessary to judge Uthman's affair, given his asceticism, piety, high standing in religion, being one of the two migrations, the son-in-law of the Messenger of God for two daughters, spending noble and valuable wealth in supporting the religion and equipping the Muslim army, being among those given glad tidings of Paradise, and the Prophet's saying about Uthman: 'He is my brother and companion in Paradise', and his saying when he covered his knee at Uthman's coming: 'Should I not feel shy of one whom the angels of heaven feel shy of?' and his saying about him and Ali when they came to him for something: 'Thus you will enter Paradise; none loves you except a believer and none hates you except a hypocrite.' And it is narrated that he said...
Source pages p. 1161

Commentary
This passage defends Uthman against the accusation that he banished Abu Dharr. It has three parts: First, it questions the historical reliability of the claim, citing al-Hasan al-Basri's denial and explanation of a possible misinterpretation. Second, it provides a reasonable justification: Uthman was wealthy and Abu Dharr, being ascetic, was critical of Uthman's lifestyle, and Uthman thought it beneficial to send him to al-Rabada to preserve the dignity of the caliphate. Third, it presents an alternative narrative from Abu Dharr himself that he left voluntarily due to a prophecy. Finally, Nasafi lays down a principle: even without these external reports, Uthman's outstanding merits—his piety, his having made two migrations, being a husband of two of the Prophet's daughters, his generous spending for Islam, being promised Paradise, and the Prophet's praise for him and Ali—oblige us to interpret his actions favorably. This establishes a precedent for defending the Companions' actions by their high moral status.

Key Terms
المبشرون بالجنة
ختن رسول الله
لا يحبكما إلا مؤمن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A Companion's actions can be judged without considering his virtue.
Correction: Nasafi argues that a Companion's high moral status obliges us to interpret ambiguous actions positively.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the Prophet say about those who love Uthman and Ali?
A) They will enter Paradise
B) They are believers
C) They are hypocrites
D) They are companions

Key Takeaway
A Companion's established virtues and the Prophet's praise require us to interpret his actions in the best possible manner.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear criticism of a believer who is known for their good deeds and sacrifices, do you immediately defend them or do you entertain the accusation? Uthman's virtues demand we judge him favorably. Is there someone in your life whom you have misjudged based on a single mistake, ignoring their years of service? Commit to seeking out their virtues and giving them the benefit of the doubt before the Day when all secrets are exposed.
?
The Prophet himself testified to Uthman's status in Paradise. Yet many still speak against him. Are you among those who base their opinions on the Prophet's testimony or on the gossip of the masses? Choose one Muslim leader or scholar whom you have spoken ill of and resolve to defend them based on their known good, even if you disagree with some of their actions.
?
If Uthman's virtues oblige us to interpret his actions in the best light, what about your own parents, teachers, or spouse? Do you grant them the same courtesy, or do you hold them to a standard of perfection? Write down one recent incident where you judged someone harshly and then rewrite the narrative assuming their good intentions and past virtues. How does that change your feelings?

The Sending of Abu Dharr to al-Rabadha
Nasafi defends Uthman's decision to send Abu Dharr to al-Rabadha as a matter of expediency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's defense of Uthman's decision to send Abu Dharr to al-Rabadha as an act of expediency rather than injustice.

Core Idea
Uthman's sending of Abu Dharr was a matter of expediency, not injustice.

In this passage, Nasafi addresses the historical controversy surrounding Uthman's treatment of Abu Dharr. He argues that Uthman's decision was based on consideration of the greater good (al-maslaha) and not arbitrary. The passage provides two narrations that justify Uthman's action.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall argument.
2
Identify the first argument
Notice how Nasafi first explains that Abu Dharr's harsh speech undermined the caliphate's dignity, leading Uthman to see sending him away as expedient.
The key term here is 'al-maslaha' (expediency).
3
Examine the second narration
Read the report about Muawiyah's complaint and Abu Dharr's refusal based on the Prophet's order. Note that Uthman gave him a choice, and he chose al-Rabadha.
This shows Abu Dharr's consent, not coercion.
4
Reflect on the misconception
Consider the common misunderstanding that Uthman exiled Abu Dharr unjustly. See how the passage addresses this with both expediency and consent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عيش الأغنياء، وكان أبو ذر يطلب منه أن يقتدي بأبي بكر وعمر - رضي الله عنهما - في رفض الزينة ومجانبة الشبهات وكان يخاشنه في الكلام في ذلك المعنى على وجه كان يذهب بهيبة الخلافة، فرأى المصلحة في أن بعثه إلى الربذة، ولا عيب في هذا، وروي أن معاوية كتب إلى عثمان يشكو أبا ذر فكتب عثمان إلى أبي ذر يستقدمه إلى المدينة، فأبى أبو ذر، وقال : سمعت رسول الله عليه السلام يقول: "إذا بلغت عمارة المدينة إلى موضع كذا فاخرج عنها" وقد بلغت العمارة ذلك الموضع فخيره عثمان أي البلاد أحب إليه ؟ فاختار الربذة، فقال له: فاخرج إليها
The life of the wealthy, and Abu Dharr was asking him to follow Abu Bakr and Umar - may God be pleased with them - in rejecting adornment and avoiding ambiguities, and he would speak harshly to him about that matter in a way that undermined the dignity of the caliphate. So he (Uthman) saw the expediency in sending him to al-Rabadha, and there is no fault in this. And it is narrated that Muawiyah wrote to Uthman complaining about Abu Dharr, so Uthman wrote to Abu Dharr summoning him to Medina, but Abu Dharr refused and said: I heard the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, say: 'When the building of Medina reaches such-and-such a place, then leave it.' And the building had reached that place. So Uthman gave him the choice of which land he preferred, and he chose al-Rabadha, so he said to him: Go out to it.
Source pages p. 1162

Commentary
This passage begins a defense of Caliph Uthman's treatment of Abu Dharr al-Ghifari. The author, Nasafi, explains that Abu Dharr was pressing Uthman to adopt the austere lifestyle of Abu Bakr and Umar, and he did so in a confrontational manner that diminished the respect owed to the caliphate. Uthman, seeing the greater good (al-maslaha), decided to send Abu Dharr to al-Rabadha, and the author asserts there is nothing blameworthy in this. Then he recounts a second narration: Muawiyah complained about Abu Dharr, so Uthman summoned him, but Abu Dharr claimed the Prophet had ordered him to leave Medina once the city's buildings reached a certain point. Since that had occurred, Uthman allowed Abu Dharr to choose his destination, and he chose al-Rabadha. The author uses these stories to show that Uthman's action was neither arbitrary nor malicious, but rather a considered response to circumstances.

Key Terms
أبو ذر
الربذة
المصلحة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Uthman exiled Abu Dharr unjustly without cause or consent.
Correction: The passage shows Uthman acted out of expediency to protect the caliphate's dignity, and Abu Dharr himself chose al-Rabadha based on a prophetic command.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did Uthman send Abu Dharr to al-Rabadha?
A) To punish him for disobeying orders
B) Because he saw it as expedient to preserve the dignity of the caliphate
C) Because Abu Dharr requested to go there
D) Because Muawiyah forced him to do so

Key Takeaway
Uthman's sending of Abu Dharr to al-Rabadha was a justified measure based on expediency and consent, not arbitrary exile.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever insisted on a righteous position so forcefully that you undermined the dignity of a leader or authority figure? How can you balance speaking truth with preserving respect in your future interactions? Commit to one practical change.
?
When you disagree with a decision made by someone in authority, do you assume their motives are corrupt? This lesson shows Uthman's decision as expedient, not unjust. What would it take for you to give leaders the benefit of the doubt? Identify one relationship where you need to make this shift.
?
Abu Dharr ultimately chose to leave Medina because of the Prophet's command. Is there a command of Allah or His Messenger that you have been resisting because it requires a difficult change? What is one step you will take this week to submit to that command?

Interpreting Uthman's Actions Through His Virtues
Nasafi cites hadiths praising Uthman to argue his actions must be interpreted favorably.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Nasafi argues that Uthman's prophetic virtues require his actions to be interpreted in the best possible light.

Core Idea
Uthman's virtues from the Prophet mandate that his actions be seen favorably.

This passage from Nasafi's work addresses a key theological and historical principle: how to evaluate the actions of a Companion like Uthman who is praised by the Prophet. Nasafi argues that given Uthman's immense merits, any ambiguity must be resolved in his favor. The following source presents the evidence for this principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the structure: a principle stated at the beginning, followed by a list of Uthman's virtues, and then a conclusion.
Pay attention to the word 'لوجب' (it would be obligatory) which introduces the main claim.
2
Identify the key principle
Nasafi starts by saying that even if nothing were narrated, it would be obligatory to interpret Uthman's affair favorably. This is the core thesis: his virtues alone mandate a favorable interpretation.
3
List Uthman's merits
The passage enumerates numerous merits: double migration, being son-in-law of the Prophet, spending wealth, being given glad tidings of Paradise, and several specific hadiths. Try to list them mentally.
4
Understand the logical conclusion
Given these merits, any action of Uthman must be interpreted in the best way. This principle is used to defend Uthman against criticisms.
5
Reflect on the purpose
Nasafi is not just praising Uthman; he is establishing a hermeneutic principle. Reflect on how this argument would be used in theological debates.
This connects to broader Sunni doctrines on the Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو لم يرو شيء من هذه الوجوه لكان الواجب حمل أمر عثمان مع زهده وورعه وجلال قدره في الدين في كونه من الذين هاجروا هجرتين، وختنا لرسول الله على الابنتين وإنفاقه في نصرة الدين وتجهيز جيش المسلمين كل نفيس وخطير من الأموال ومضنون به من النعم، وكونه من المبشرين بالجنة، وقول النبي عليه السلام فيه عثمان "أخي ورفيقي في الجنة" وقوله عليه السلام - لما ستر ركبته عند مجيء عثمان -: "ألا أستحي ممن تستحي منه ملائكة السماء"، وقوله عليه السلام فيه وفي علي رضي الله عنهما لما أتياه في شيء: "هكذا تدخلان الجنة لا يحبكما إلا مؤمن ولا يبغضكما إلا منافق" وروي أنه عليه السلام قال في عثمان تدخل الجنة بغير حساب وحكمه له بأنه يقتل شهيدًا، وأمره له بأن لا يخلع ثوبا كساه الله إياه. في أخبار كثيرة يطول ذكرها
And even if nothing of these aspects had been narrated, it would be obligatory to interpret the affair of Uthman, given his asceticism, piety, and high standing in religion, his being among those who migrated twice, his being the son-in-law of the Messenger of God to two daughters, his spending in support of the religion and equipping the army of the Muslims with every precious and valuable possession and cherished blessing, his being among those given glad tidings of Paradise, and the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him, about Uthman: 'My brother and companion in Paradise,' and his saying, peace be upon him—when he covered his knee upon Uthman's arrival—'Should I not be shy of one whom the angels of heaven are shy of?' and his saying, peace be upon him, about him and Ali, may God be pleased with them both, when they came to him about something: 'Thus you both enter Paradise; none loves you except a believer, and none hates you except a hypocrite,' and it is narrated that he, peace be upon him, said about Uthman: 'You will enter Paradise without reckoning,' and his judgment that he would be killed as a martyr, and his order that he should not remove a garment that God had clothed him with, in many reports that would be lengthy to mention.
Source pages p. 1162

Commentary
This passage presents a principle for interpreting Uthman's actions. The author, Nasafi, argues that even if no overt excuses existed, the overwhelming virtues of Uthman mandate that his actions be interpreted in the best possible light. He enumerates Uthman's merits: his asceticism and piety, his high rank in religion, his double migration (to Abyssinia and Medina), being the husband of two of the Prophet's daughters, his immense spending for the sake of Islam and to equip the army, his being one of the ten promised Paradise, and specific hadiths in which the Prophet calls him 'my brother and companion in Paradise,' says that the angels are shy of him, declares that only a believer loves him and Ali, asserts that he will enter Paradise without reckoning, foresees his martyrdom, and commands him not to remove a garment God gave him (interpreted as not resigning the caliphate). These honors establish that any criticism of Uthman must be resolved in his favor. The passage then transitions to addressing specific accusations.

Key Terms
المبشرون بالجنة
الهجرتان
الصهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Uthman's actions can be critically judged without considering his prophetic commendations.
Correction: Nasafi argues that Uthman's virtues, especially the Prophet's explicit praises, require us to interpret his actions in the best possible light, not to judge them harshly.

Checkpoint

A) They are among the ten promised Paradise
B) Love for them is a sign of faith and hatred a sign of hypocrisy
C) They are the best of the Companions
D) They were married to the Prophet's daughters

Key Takeaway
Nasafi's argument shows that prophetic commendation must shape our understanding of a Companion's actions, mandating a favorable interpretation.

?

Refutation of the Charge of Favoritism Toward Relatives
Nasafi argues Uthman gave to relatives from his own wealth, not public funds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi defends Uthman by distinguishing between personal and public wealth and using the Companions' silent approval as evidence.

Core Idea
Uthman gave from his own wealth, not the public treasury.

In defending Uthman against accusations of nepotism, Nasafi presents a two-part argument: first, that Uthman was wealthy and gave from his own money, and second, that the Companions' lack of objection proves the gifts were not from public funds. This passage illustrates how historical facts and communal consensus are used in theological defense. We will examine the logic and evidence Nasafi employs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then the English translation. Notice the structure: accusation, then defense, then supporting evidence.
The passage is a single sentence in Arabic, but contains a complete argument.
2
Identify the two parts of the defense
Nasafi first states that Uthman gave from his own wealth, then cites the Companions' silence as proof. Break down these two points.
3
Understand the argument from silence
The absence of criticism from the Companions is taken as evidence that the gifts were legitimate. Consider why this is a strong argument in Sunni theology.
The Companions' consensus (ijma) is a key source of authority.
4
Reflect on the broader significance
This defense protects Uthman's reputation and reinforces the principle that leaders may use personal wealth freely, but must not misuse public funds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما يزعمون أنه كان يؤثر أهله ويعطيهم أموالاً جمة، فذلك محمول على أنه كان يعطيهم من ماله إذ هو الله كان ذا مال كثير، ولهذا لم يرو النكير عليه من الصحابة، ولو كان يعطي من مال المسلمين لأنكروا ذلك عليه
And what they claim, that he favored his family and gave them abundant wealth, that is to be interpreted as that he gave them from his own wealth, since he, may God be pleased with him, was a man of great wealth, and for this reason no disapproval was narrated from the Companions against him; had he been giving from the wealth of the Muslims, they would have denounced that against him.
Source pages p. 1163

Commentary
This passage answers the accusation that Caliph Uthman practiced nepotism by giving large sums of money to his relatives. The author, Nasafi, explains that the proper understanding is that Uthman gave from his personal wealth, because Uthman was independently wealthy. He supports this by noting that none of the Companions are recorded as objecting to his gifts. If Uthman had been giving from the public treasury (the wealth of the Muslims), the Companions would certainly have criticized him. Their silence indicates that the money was his own. Thus the accusation is refuted by appealing to the consensus of the Companions' tacit approval.

Key Terms
تأثير الأهل
مال المسلمين
النكير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Uthman gave public funds to his relatives.
Correction: Nasafi asserts that Uthman gave from his personal wealth, as supported by his wealth and the Companions' lack of objection.

Checkpoint
How does Nasafi refute the claim that Uthman gave public money to his relatives?
A) By saying Uthman was wealthy and gave from his own money, as shown by lack of Companion disapproval
B) By denying the accusation outright
C) By saying the relatives deserved it
D) By claiming the narrations are weak

Key Takeaway
Nasafi defends Uthman by asserting he used personal wealth and by invoking the Companions' silent approval as evidence of propriety.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear an accusation against someone, do you instinctively assume the worst? How can Uthman's defense—seeking the proper interpretation and evidence—change your own reaction? Will you commit to investigating before judging, even if the accused is disliked?
?
Uthman gave generously from his own wealth. Are you generous with your resources, or do you hold back? Examine your spending this week: is it for Allah's sake or for yourself? What is one concrete act of giving you can do today from your own wealth?
?
The Companions' silence is used as proof of approval. In your life, when you see a wrong, do you speak up or stay silent? Is your silence due to trust, fear, or indifference? How can you ensure your silence does not become complicity? This week, identify one situation where you must speak and commit to doing so.

Refutation of the Claim That Companions Abandoned Uthman
Nasafi explains Uthman's refusal to fight and notes Companions offered themselves.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's argument that Uthman chose not to fight the rebels out of mercy and that the Companions offered their support, countering the accusation of abandonment.

Core Idea
Uthman's restraint prevented civil war; Companions were not negligent.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi directly confronts a historical accusation that the Companions collectively deserted Uthman during his siege. He offers an alternative narrative: Uthman himself refused to fight to avoid Muslim bloodshed, and the Emigrants and Helpers actually volunteered to defend him. This lesson unpacks the text and its refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: first the accusation, then the response.
The passage ends abruptly; focus on the argument presented.
2
Identify the accusation
The first part describes the claim that the Companions sat back and abandoned Uthman until he was killed and left unburied, with only insignificant people attending to him.
3
Understand Uthman's reasoning
The second part explains Uthman's motive: he refrained from fighting out of compassion and to avoid shedding Muslim blood, also to avoid the perception that he used force against complainants.
This shows Uthman's piety and strategic thinking.
4
Note the Companions' response
The passage states that the Emigrants and Helpers offered themselves to Uthman for defense. This refutes the claim that they abandoned him.
The text implies Uthman declined their offer.
5
Reflect on the refutation
Consider how the passage turns the accusation on its head: the Companions were willing, but Uthman chose restraint.
This is a key argument in defending the Companions' honor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما يذكرون أن أصحاب رسول الله عليه السلام قعدوا عنه وخذلوه حتى قتل وترك ثلاثا لا يدفن، ثم لم يتبعه ولم يتول أمره إلا من لا يؤبه به. فيقال: إن عثمان الله كان يمتنع عن قتالهم شفقة منه على الخلق وتوقيًا عن إراقة دماء المسلمين وكراهية أن يقال: إن قوماً جاءوا متظلمين من عامل له فأساء إليهم وقصد سفك دمائهم، وكان المهاجرون والأنصار يعرضون أنفسهم عليه
And what they mention, that the Companions of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, sat back and abandoned him until he was killed and left three days unburied, then no one followed him and no one took charge of his affair except someone insignificant. It is said: Indeed, Uthman, may God be pleased with him, was refraining from fighting them out of compassion for creation and caution against shedding the blood of Muslims, and disliking that it be said that a people came complaining about a governor appointed by him, and he acted badly toward them and intended to shed their blood. And the Emigrants and Helpers were offering themselves to him.
Source pages p. 1163

Commentary
This passage addresses the accusation that the Companions collectively failed Uthman during his siege, leaving him unsupported for three days after his death. The author, Nasafi, provides a counter-narrative: Uthman himself chose not to fight the rebels out of mercy and concern for Muslim lives, and because he did not want to be seen as using force against people who claimed to be wronged by his governor. Moreover, the Emigrants (Muhajirun) and Helpers (Ansar) actually presented themselves to him, offering to defend him. The implication is that Uthman refused their help to avoid bloodshed. The passage, though cut off, argues that the Companions were not negligent; rather, Uthman's own decision led to the situation.

Key Terms
خذلان
شفقة
المهاجرون والأنصار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Companions abandoned Uthman and left him to die without support.
Correction: Uthman refused to fight to avoid civil war, and the Companions (Emigrants and Helpers) offered to defend him, but he declined their offer.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did Uthman refrain from fighting the rebels?
A) Because he was weak and had no support
B) Out of compassion and to avoid Muslim bloodshed
C) Because he knew he would be killed anyway
D) Because the Companions refused to fight

Key Takeaway
Uthman's restraint and the Companions' willingness to defend him demonstrate that the accusation of abandonment is unfounded.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you been falsely accused, and did you respond with Uthman's kind of restraint or with defensive anger? What would it cost you to choose compassion over proving yourself right?
?
The Companions were ready to fight for Uthman, but he refused to shed Muslim blood. Is there a situation in your life where you are willing to sacrifice your own 'victory' to protect the unity of others? What would that look like practically this week?
?
Uthman's motive was not weakness but deep concern for the ummah. Do you truly believe that sometimes the strongest, most courageous act is to hold back and absorb the blame? Examine your heart: do you seek justice or do you seek your own vindication?

Prophetic Testimonies for Uthman's Honor
Author cites prophetic testimonies to mandate favorable interpretation of Uthman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses prophetic reports to establish that Uthman's actions must be interpreted in the best light.

Core Idea
Prophetic praise mandates interpreting Uthman's actions favorably.

The author begins by invoking powerful prophetic statements about Uthman's status in Paradise and the future of the caliphate. These form the foundation for a principled defense: if the Prophet himself guaranteed Uthman's excellence, then any accusation against him must be examined with extreme caution and reinterpreted in a way befitting his rank. In this lesson, you will see how these reports set the hermeneutic rule for all that follows.

Guided Path
1
Read the prophetic reports
Read the Arabic passage containing the reports about Uthman entering Paradise without reckoning, being killed as a martyr, and the command not to remove a garment.
These reports are the author's primary evidence.
2
Understand the hermeneutic principle
The author argues that since the Prophet declared the caliphate thirty years, Uthman's reign is validated, so his actions must be interpreted in the best way.
This principle guides the entire defense.
3
Reflect on the rhetorical question
The author asks how, given these proofs, anyone could interpret Uthman's actions in the ugliest way. Consider the strength of this rhetorical move.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في عثمان تدخل الجنة بغير حساب وحكمه له بأنه يقتل شهيدًا، وأمره له بأن لا يخلع ثوبا كساه الله إياه. في أخبار كثيرة يطول ذكرها ، ومع قول النبي عليه السلام: "الخلافة بعدي ثلاثون سنة" لكان الواجب حمل أمره على وجه يليق بشأنه وجلال قدره، فكيف يجوز مع وجود هذه المعاني والأخبار حمل أمره على أقبح الوجوه وأفسدها؟!! وقد روي في تأويل ما فعل هذه الوجوه الصحيحة التي توجب دفع الطعن عنه. وما يزعمون أنه كان يؤثر أهله ويعطيهم أموالاً جمة، فذلك محمول على أنه كان يعطيهم من ماله إذ هو كان ذا مال كثير، ولهذا لم يرو النكير عليه من الصحابة، ولو كان يعطي من مال المسلمين لأنكروا ذلك عليه. وما يذكرون أن أصحاب رسول الله عليه السلام قعدوا عنه وخذلوه حتى قتل وترك ثلاثا لا يدفن، ثم لم يتبعه ولم يتول أمره إلا من لا يؤبه به. فيقال: إن عثمان كان يمتنع عن قتالهم شفقة منه على الخلق وتوقيًا عن إراقة دماء المسلمين وكراهية أن يقال: إن قوماً جاءوا متظلمين من عامل له فأساء إليهم وقصد سفك دمائهم، وكان المهاجرون والأنصار يعرضون أنفسهم عليه ويسألون منه أن يأذن لهم في محاربتهم، فكان يمتنع عن ذلك لما مر من المعاني ذلك كان الحسن والحسين وقنبر - رضي الله عنهم - حضروا الدار ودفعوا حتى خرجوا وعقروا ولم يكن عنده ولا عند أحد من الصحابة – رضي الله عنهم - أن الأمر يبلغ ذلك المبلغ ولكن نفذ فيه قضاء الله المحتوم ونالته الشهادة التي كتبت له. وما قالوا: أنه انه ترك ثلاثاً فإنه لا يصح ذلك البتة، وكيف يظن بالمهاجرين والأنصار - رضي الله عنهم - وخصوصا بعلي ولو مات بجوارهم يهودي أو نصراني ما كانوا يرضون بأن يتركوه حرز السباع لا يوارون سوأته ولا يسترون عورته، فكيف جوزوا ذلك في عثمان مع سابقته في الإسلام وآثاره في الدين واتصاله برسول الله بابنتيه وبشارة النبي عليه السلام إياه بالجنة، فهذا والله هو الطعن الظاهر على الصحابة عموماً وعلى على خصوصا، ولو ثبت ذلك لكان الطعن بذلك عائدًا على من استجاز ذلك في مثله لا إليه إلا أن يكونوا تشاغلوا بعقد الإمامة وتسكين الفتنة خوفًا على الناس أن يتشتتوا وتتفرق كلمتهم، فيوجب حدوث ذلك وهنا في الإسلام، ثم تفرغوا بعد ذلك لأمره وأخذوا في تجهيزه ودفنه رضوان الله عليه. وما يروون أنه كتب يوم الحصار إلى علي: فإن كنت مأكولاً فكن خير آكل وإلا فأدركني ولما أمزق - فلا أصل له إذ المعروف من أمر عثمان أنه كان يتحامى من الحرب ويتجوز عن ذلك حتى قال: من وضع السلاح من غلماني فهو حر. ومن كان هذا - مع من قصد الحرب من غلمانه - فعله فكيف
Concerning Uthman: he enters Paradise without reckoning, and his judgment that he will be killed as a martyr, and his command to him not to remove a garment which God had clothed him with. There are many reports whose mention would be long. And with the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'The caliphate after me is thirty years,' it would be obligatory to interpret his affair in a manner befitting his status and the majesty of his rank. So how is it permissible, with the existence of these meanings and reports, to interpret his affair in the ugliest and most corrupt ways?!! And it has been narrated in interpretation of what he did, these sound ways that require warding off criticism from him. And what they claim that he favored his family and gave them abundant wealth, that is interpreted as that he gave them from his own wealth, for he indeed possessed much wealth, and for this reason no disapproval was reported from the Companions against him. Had he been giving from the wealth of the Muslims, they would have disapproved of that against him. And what they mention that the Companions of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, withdrew from him and abandoned him until he was killed, and he was left (unburied) for three (days) not buried, then no one followed him and undertook his affair except those not regarded. So it is said: Indeed, Uthman refrained from fighting them out of compassion for creation and caution about shedding the blood of Muslims, and dislike that it be said: A group came complaining about an official of his, and he treated them badly and intended to shed their blood. And the Muhajirun and Ansar were offering themselves to him and asking him to permit them to fight them, but he refrained from that due to the meanings mentioned. That was when al-Hasan, al-Husayn, and Qanbar - may God be pleased with them - attended the house and fought until they went out and were wounded. And it was not in his view nor in the view of any of the Companions - may God be pleased with them - that the matter would reach that extent, but God's decreed decree was executed upon him and he attained the martyrdom that was written for him. And what they said: that he was left for three (days) - indeed that is not correct at all. How could it be thought of the Muhajirun and Ansar - may God be pleased with them - and especially Ali - may God be pleased with him - that if a Jew or Christian died near them, they would not be pleased that he be left as a prey for beasts, not covering his private parts nor concealing his nakedness? So how could they permit that in the case of Uthman, with his precedence in Islam, his effects in the religion, his connection to the Messenger of God through his two daughters, and the Prophet's giving him glad tidings of Paradise? This, by God, is an open criticism of the Companions in general and of Ali in particular. And if that were established, the criticism would return upon whoever permitted that in the likes of him, not upon him. Unless they were occupied with the appointment of the Imam and calming the turmoil, fearing for the people that they would scatter and their word become divided, causing weakness in Islam. Then after that they attended to his affair and began preparing him and burying him, may God be pleased with him. And what they narrate that he wrote on the day of the siege to Ali: 'If I am to be eaten, then be the best eater; otherwise reach me before I am torn apart' - this has no basis. For what is known from the affair of Uthman is that he was averse to war and avoided it, even saying: 'Whoever of my slaves lays down his weapon is free.' And he who did this with those who intended war from his slaves - how
Source pages p. 1163

Commentary
This passage is a refutation and defense of Caliph Uthman ibn Affan against several accusations. The author presents a series of responses to criticisms about Uthman's actions and the behavior of the Companions during the events leading to his death. The argument follows the order of the accusations:

1. First, the author cites prophetic reports that Uthman will enter Paradise without reckoning and be killed as a martyr, and the Prophet's command not to remove a garment God clothed him with. Given the Prophet's statement that the caliphate after him is thirty years (which includes Uthman's reign), it is obligatory to interpret Uthman's actions in the best possible light. The author questions how, with these proofs, anyone could interpret Uthman's actions in the worst way.

2. Regarding the accusation that Uthman favored his family and gave them abundant wealth, the author argues that he gave from his own wealth, not from the public treasury, because he was wealthy. If it had been from Muslim wealth, the other Companions would have objected, but no such objection is recorded.

3. As for the claim that the Companions abandoned Uthman, leaving him unburied for three days, the author explains that Uthman himself refrained from fighting out of mercy and aversion to bloodshed. The Muhajirun and Ansar offered to fight but he refused. Even al-Hasan, al-Husayn, and Qanbar fought at the house but were wounded. No one expected the siege to reach that level, but God's decree was executed. The claim that his body was left unburied for three days is false. It is unthinkable that the Muhajirun and Ansar, especially Ali, would leave even a Jew or Christian unburied, so how could they do that to Uthman given his virtues? If such neglect occurred, the blame would fall on those who allowed it, not on Uthman; or perhaps they were busy with appointing a new leader and calming the situation to prevent the collapse of the community, after which they tended to his burial.

4. Finally, the story that Uthman wrote to Ali saying 'If I am to be eaten, be the best eater; otherwise reach me before I am torn' is baseless. Uthman was known to be averse to war; he freed any slave who laid down weapons. So how could he write such a call for aid? The passage ends mid-sentence.

The style is argumentative, using rhetorical questions and logical inferences to defend Uthman and the honor of the Companions.

Key Terms
عثمان
الشهادة
الخلافة
تأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Uthman's actions are open to negative interpretation because he was a human being.
Correction: The prophetic reports elevate Uthman's status to the level that his actions must be interpreted in the best possible way.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for insisting that Uthman's actions be interpreted favorably?
A) His wealth and status
B) The reports of the Prophet about him and the thirty-year caliphate
C) The consensus of later scholars
D) The opinion of his family

Key Takeaway
Prophetic testimonies about Uthman's honor require that his actions be understood in the best possible light.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear negative reports about a person whom the Prophet has praised, do you immediately assume the worst? What would it take for you to actively seek a favorable interpretation, as this lesson obligates for Uthman?
?
Think of someone in your life whom you have judged harshly. If that person had received explicit praise from the Prophet, would you still hold your negative judgment? What does that tell you about your own tendency to assume ill?
?
The Prophet commanded Uthman not to remove the garment of authority that Allah clothed him with. Are you tempted to 'remove' the authority or honor of someone you dislike? How can you apply the principle of favorable interpretation to that person starting today?

Refuting the Accusation of Misusing Public Wealth
Author refutes accusation of misusing public wealth by asserting personal wealth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's argument that Uthman gave from his personal wealth, not the treasury.

Core Idea
Uthman gave from his own wealth, not from the Muslims' treasury.

One of the common accusations against Uthman is that he favored his Umayyad relatives by giving them large sums from the public treasury. The author responds by pointing out that Uthman was personally wealthy and that no Companion objected—which would have happened if public funds were misused. This lesson examines that argument closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the accusation and response
Read the Arabic passage that states the accusation and the author's response.
Note the structure: claim then refutation.
2
Identify the key point
The author argues that Uthman gave from his own wealth. Identify the evidence given: his personal wealth and the lack of objection from Companions.
3
Evaluate the logical inference
Consider why the lack of objection is a strong argument. What does it imply about the norms of the time?
Companions were known to speak truth to power.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage is a refutation and defense of Caliph Uthman ibn Affan against several accusations. The author presents a series of responses to criticisms about Uthman's actions and the behavior of the Companions during the events leading to his death. The argument follows the order of the accusations:

1. First, the author cites prophetic reports that Uthman will enter Paradise without reckoning and be killed as a martyr, and the Prophet's command not to remove a garment God clothed him with. Given the Prophet's statement that the caliphate after him is thirty years (which includes Uthman's reign), it is obligatory to interpret Uthman's actions in the best possible light. The author questions how, with these proofs, anyone could interpret Uthman's actions in the worst way.

2. Regarding the accusation that Uthman favored his family and gave them abundant wealth, the author argues that he gave from his own wealth, not from the public treasury, because he was wealthy. If it had been from Muslim wealth, the other Companions would have objected, but no such objection is recorded.

3. As for the claim that the Companions abandoned Uthman, leaving him unburied for three days, the author explains that Uthman himself refrained from fighting out of mercy and aversion to bloodshed. The Muhajirun and Ansar offered to fight but he refused. Even al-Hasan, al-Husayn, and Qanbar fought at the house but were wounded. No one expected the siege to reach that level, but God's decree was executed. The claim that his body was left unburied for three days is false. It is unthinkable that the Muhajirun and Ansar, especially Ali, would leave even a Jew or Christian unburied, so how could they do that to Uthman given his virtues? If such neglect occurred, the blame would fall on those who allowed it, not on Uthman; or perhaps they were busy with appointing a new leader and calming the situation to prevent the collapse of the community, after which they tended to his burial.

4. Finally, the story that Uthman wrote to Ali saying 'If I am to be eaten, be the best eater; otherwise reach me before I am torn' is baseless. Uthman was known to be averse to war; he freed any slave who laid down weapons. So how could he write such a call for aid? The passage ends mid-sentence.

The style is argumentative, using rhetorical questions and logical inferences to defend Uthman and the honor of the Companions.

Key Terms
عثمان
الطعن
تأويل
الصحابة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Uthman used public funds to enrich his relatives.
Correction: The author says he gave from his private wealth, and the silence of the Companions supports this.

Checkpoint
What is the author's main argument for why Uthman's gifts to his family were not from the treasury?
A) Uthman was poor and couldn't give from treasury
B) The Companions would have objected if public funds were used
C) The Prophet ordered him to do so
D) The recipients were not his family

Key Takeaway
Uthman gave from his own wealth, and the lack of Companion objection confirms this.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear an accusation against someone, do you immediately assume guilt, or do you seek evidence as the author does here? What practical step can you take this week to verify a claim before believing it?
?
Uthman gave generously from his own wealth. Are you generous with what Allah has given you, or do you hold back fearing loss? How can you give from your own resources to benefit others today?
?
The Companions' silence is used as proof of Uthman's innocence. Is your silence when witnessing wrongdoing a sign of approval? Examine your heart: when do you stay silent when you should speak up for justice?

Refuting Abandonment and Delayed Burial
Author refutes accusations of abandonment and delayed burial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's response to the accusation that the Companions abandoned Uthman and left him unburied for three days.

Core Idea
Companions did not abandon Uthman; they were occupied with preserving unity.

The most painful accusation is that the Companions, including Ali, abandoned Uthman and even left his body unburied for three days. The author offers a detailed refutation: Uthman himself forbade fighting, the Muhajirun and Ansar offered help but he refused, and the delay in burial was due to the pressing need to appoint a new leader to prevent civil war. This lesson unpacks these arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the charge and initial response
Read the Arabic passage that presents the charge that Companions abandoned Uthman and left him unburied, and the author's immediate response.
The response begins with 'فيقال'.
2
Understand Uthman's stance
The author explains why Uthman refrained from fighting: compassion and fear of causing division.
This shows Uthman's piety.
3
Analyze the burial delay explanation
The author refutes the three-day delay as false, then offers a possible excuse: the Companions were busy stabilizing the caliphate.
This preserves the honor of the Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في عثمان تدخل الجنة بغير حساب وحكمه له بأنه يقتل شهيدًا، وأمره له بأن لا يخلع ثوبا كساه الله إياه. في أخبار كثيرة يطول ذكرها ، ومع قول النبي عليه السلام: "الخلافة بعدي ثلاثون سنة" لكان الواجب حمل أمره على وجه يليق بشأنه وجلال قدره، فكيف يجوز مع وجود هذه المعاني والأخبار حمل أمره على أقبح الوجوه وأفسدها؟!! وقد روي في تأويل ما فعل هذه الوجوه الصحيحة التي توجب دفع الطعن عنه. وما يزعمون أنه كان يؤثر أهله ويعطيهم أموالاً جمة، فذلك محمول على أنه كان يعطيهم من ماله إذ هو كان ذا مال كثير، ولهذا لم يرو النكير عليه من الصحابة، ولو كان يعطي من مال المسلمين لأنكروا ذلك عليه. وما يذكرون أن أصحاب رسول الله عليه السلام قعدوا عنه وخذلوه حتى قتل وترك ثلاثا لا يدفن، ثم لم يتبعه ولم يتول أمره إلا من لا يؤبه به. فيقال: إن عثمان كان يمتنع عن قتالهم شفقة منه على الخلق وتوقيًا عن إراقة دماء المسلمين وكراهية أن يقال: إن قوماً جاءوا متظلمين من عامل له فأساء إليهم وقصد سفك دمائهم، وكان المهاجرون والأنصار يعرضون أنفسهم عليه ويسألون منه أن يأذن لهم في محاربتهم، فكان يمتنع عن ذلك لما مر من المعاني ذلك كان الحسن والحسين وقنبر - رضي الله عنهم - حضروا الدار ودفعوا حتى خرجوا وعقروا ولم يكن عنده ولا عند أحد من الصحابة – رضي الله عنهم - أن الأمر يبلغ ذلك المبلغ ولكن نفذ فيه قضاء الله المحتوم ونالته الشهادة التي كتبت له. وما قالوا: أنه انه ترك ثلاثاً فإنه لا يصح ذلك البتة، وكيف يظن بالمهاجرين والأنصار - رضي الله عنهم - وخصوصا بعلي ولو مات بجوارهم يهودي أو نصراني ما كانوا يرضون بأن يتركوه حرز السباع لا يوارون سوأته ولا يسترون عورته، فكيف جوزوا ذلك في عثمان مع سابقته في الإسلام وآثاره في الدين واتصاله برسول الله بابنتيه وبشارة النبي عليه السلام إياه بالجنة، فهذا والله هو الطعن الظاهر على الصحابة عموماً وعلى على خصوصا، ولو ثبت ذلك لكان الطعن بذلك عائدًا على من استجاز ذلك في مثله لا إليه إلا أن يكونوا تشاغلوا بعقد الإمامة وتسكين الفتنة خوفًا على الناس أن يتشتتوا وتتفرق كلمتهم، فيوجب حدوث ذلك وهنا في الإسلام، ثم تفرغوا بعد ذلك لأمره وأخذوا في تجهيزه ودفنه رضوان الله عليه. وما يروون أنه كتب يوم الحصار إلى علي: فإن كنت مأكولاً فكن خير آكل وإلا فأدركني ولما أمزق - فلا أصل له إذ المعروف من أمر عثمان أنه كان يتحامى من الحرب ويتجوز عن ذلك حتى قال: من وضع السلاح من غلماني فهو حر. ومن كان هذا - مع من قصد الحرب من غلمانه - فعله فكيف
Concerning Uthman: he enters Paradise without reckoning, and his judgment that he will be killed as a martyr, and his command to him not to remove a garment which God had clothed him with. There are many reports whose mention would be long. And with the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'The caliphate after me is thirty years,' it would be obligatory to interpret his affair in a manner befitting his status and the majesty of his rank. So how is it permissible, with the existence of these meanings and reports, to interpret his affair in the ugliest and most corrupt ways?!! And it has been narrated in interpretation of what he did, these sound ways that require warding off criticism from him. And what they claim that he favored his family and gave them abundant wealth, that is interpreted as that he gave them from his own wealth, for he indeed possessed much wealth, and for this reason no disapproval was reported from the Companions against him. Had he been giving from the wealth of the Muslims, they would have disapproved of that against him. And what they mention that the Companions of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, withdrew from him and abandoned him until he was killed, and he was left (unburied) for three (days) not buried, then no one followed him and undertook his affair except those not regarded. So it is said: Indeed, Uthman refrained from fighting them out of compassion for creation and caution about shedding the blood of Muslims, and dislike that it be said: A group came complaining about an official of his, and he treated them badly and intended to shed their blood. And the Muhajirun and Ansar were offering themselves to him and asking him to permit them to fight them, but he refrained from that due to the meanings mentioned. That was when al-Hasan, al-Husayn, and Qanbar - may God be pleased with them - attended the house and fought until they went out and were wounded. And it was not in his view nor in the view of any of the Companions - may God be pleased with them - that the matter would reach that extent, but God's decreed decree was executed upon him and he attained the martyrdom that was written for him. And what they said: that he was left for three (days) - indeed that is not correct at all. How could it be thought of the Muhajirun and Ansar - may God be pleased with them - and especially Ali - may God be pleased with him - that if a Jew or Christian died near them, they would not be pleased that he be left as a prey for beasts, not covering his private parts nor concealing his nakedness? So how could they permit that in the case of Uthman, with his precedence in Islam, his effects in the religion, his connection to the Messenger of God through his two daughters, and the Prophet's giving him glad tidings of Paradise? This, by God, is an open criticism of the Companions in general and of Ali in particular. And if that were established, the criticism would return upon whoever permitted that in the likes of him, not upon him. Unless they were occupied with the appointment of the Imam and calming the turmoil, fearing for the people that they would scatter and their word become divided, causing weakness in Islam. Then after that they attended to his affair and began preparing him and burying him, may God be pleased with him. And what they narrate that he wrote on the day of the siege to Ali: 'If I am to be eaten, then be the best eater; otherwise reach me before I am torn apart' - this has no basis. For what is known from the affair of Uthman is that he was averse to war and avoided it, even saying: 'Whoever of my slaves lays down his weapon is free.' And he who did this with those who intended war from his slaves - how

Commentary
This passage is a refutation and defense of Caliph Uthman ibn Affan against several accusations. The author presents a series of responses to criticisms about Uthman's actions and the behavior of the Companions during the events leading to his death. The argument follows the order of the accusations:

1. First, the author cites prophetic reports that Uthman will enter Paradise without reckoning and be killed as a martyr, and the Prophet's command not to remove a garment God clothed him with. Given the Prophet's statement that the caliphate after him is thirty years (which includes Uthman's reign), it is obligatory to interpret Uthman's actions in the best possible light. The author questions how, with these proofs, anyone could interpret Uthman's actions in the worst way.

2. Regarding the accusation that Uthman favored his family and gave them abundant wealth, the author argues that he gave from his own wealth, not from the public treasury, because he was wealthy. If it had been from Muslim wealth, the other Companions would have objected, but no such objection is recorded.

3. As for the claim that the Companions abandoned Uthman, leaving him unburied for three days, the author explains that Uthman himself refrained from fighting out of mercy and aversion to bloodshed. The Muhajirun and Ansar offered to fight but he refused. Even al-Hasan, al-Husayn, and Qanbar fought at the house but were wounded. No one expected the siege to reach that level, but God's decree was executed. The claim that his body was left unburied for three days is false. It is unthinkable that the Muhajirun and Ansar, especially Ali, would leave even a Jew or Christian unburied, so how could they do that to Uthman given his virtues? If such neglect occurred, the blame would fall on those who allowed it, not on Uthman; or perhaps they were busy with appointing a new leader and calming the situation to prevent the collapse of the community, after which they tended to his burial.

4. Finally, the story that Uthman wrote to Ali saying 'If I am to be eaten, be the best eater; otherwise reach me before I am torn' is baseless. Uthman was known to be averse to war; he freed any slave who laid down weapons. So how could he write such a call for aid? The passage ends mid-sentence.

The style is argumentative, using rhetorical questions and logical inferences to defend Uthman and the honor of the Companions.

الأنصار
علي
الشهادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Companions abandoned Uthman because they were displeased with him.
Correction: They did not abandon him; they were held back by Uthman's own wishes, and the burial delay (if any) was due to political necessity.

Checkpoint
How does the author explain the possible delay in burying Uthman?
A) They were busy with the appointment of a new caliph
B) They didn't care about him
C) They were waiting for his family
D) The body was lost

Key Takeaway
The Companions did not abandon Uthman; the delay in burial (if any) was due to preserving the unity of the ummah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were in the position of the Companions during the siege of Uthman, would you have prioritized fighting for justice or obeying Uthman’s command to avoid bloodshed? What does your answer reveal about your trust in Allah’s decree over visible outcomes?
?
When you see a Muslim leader wronged and others silent, do you assume the worst of those who are silent, or do you consider that they may be working to prevent greater harm? How can you train yourself to give the benefit of the doubt like the author does for the Companions?
?
The Companions were so careful about the believers' dignity that they would not leave even a Jew or Christian unburied. What does this teach you about your own attitude toward the basic rights of others, especially those you disagree with? Commit to one concrete way you will honor the dignity of someone in your life this week.

Refuting the Letter to Ali Accusation
Author refutes alleged letter from Uthman to Ali as baseless.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's dismissal of the story that Uthman wrote a desperate letter to Ali.

Core Idea
The alleged letter to Ali is baseless and contradicts Uthman's known aversion to war.

A particularly damaging accusation is that Uthman wrote a verse to Ali calling for help, implying a conspiratorial plea. The author dismisses this as a fabrication, pointing out that it contradicts Uthman's well-known attitude of avoiding war—he even promised freedom to any slave who laid down weapons. This lesson shows how the author uses historical consistency to reject the story.

Guided Path
1
Read the alleged letter
Read the Arabic passage that presents the claim and the author's refutation.
The verse is quoted: 'If I am to be eaten...'
2
Identify the basis for rejection
The author says the story has no basis (la asl lahu) and gives evidence from Uthman's character.
3
Consider the argument from consistency
Uthman freed any slave who laid down weapons. How could he then write urging Ali to fight? This inconsistency shows the story is false.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a story about a respected figure that contradicts their known character, do you pause to verify or do you accept it? How can you train yourself to be more critical of such reports, just as this lesson teaches you to reject the letter based on character consistency?
?
Uthman's aversion to war led him to free any slave who laid down his weapon. How does your own approach to conflict reflect your deepest values? Are there areas in your life where your actions contradict what you claim to believe?
?
This lesson shows that a single fabricated story can distort history for centuries. What responsibility do you have in your own conversations to ensure you do not spread unverified claims about others, especially about the Sahaba?

Refuting the Allegation that Uthman Was Left Unburied
Refutes the allegation that Uthman was left unburied for three days.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the claim that Uthman was left unburied for three days and defends the honor of the Companions.

Core Idea
The Companions would never neglect Uthman's burial; any delay was due to necessity.

A common smear against the Companions is that they left Caliph Uthman unburied for three days. The author addresses this directly, offering both a logical refutation and a plausible explanation. Read on to see how he defends their honor.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the author's tone and the flow from narrative to refutation.
2
Identify the refutation's main points
Find where the author says the claim is 'absolutely not correct' and note the rhetorical question about a Jew or Christian. Then see the excuse about the imamate.
3
Reflect on the author's strategy
Consider why the author uses a comparison with non-Muslims and mentions Uthman's virtues. How does this strengthen the refutation?
The argument appeals to both logic and emotion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسألون منه أن يأذن لهم في محاربتهم، فكان يمتنع عن ذلك لما مر من المعاني ذلك كان الحسن والحسين وقنبر - رضي الله عنهم - حضروا الدار ودفعوا حتى خرجوا وعقروا ولم يكن عنده ولا عند أحد من الصحابة – رضي الله عنهم - أن الأمر يبلغ ذلك المبلغ ولكن نفذ فيه قضاء الله المحتوم ونالته الشهادة التي كتبت له. وما قالوا: أنه ترك ثلاثاً فإنه لا يصح ذلك البتة، وكيف يظن بالمهاجرين والأنصار - رضي الله عنهم - وخصوصا بعلي رضي الله عنه ولو مات بجوارهم يهودي أو نصراني ما كانوا يرضون بأن يتركوه حرز السباع لا يوارون سوأته ولا يسترون عورته، فكيف جوزوا ذلك في عثمان مع سابقته في الإسلام وآثاره في الدين واتصاله برسول الله بابنتيه وبشارة النبي عليه السلام إياه بالجنة، فهذا والله هو الطعن الظاهر على الصحابة عموماً وعلى علي خصوصا، ولو ثبت ذلك لكان الطعن بذلك عائداً على من استجاز ذلك في مثله لا إليه إلا أن يكونوا تشاغلوا بعقد الإمامة وتسكين الفتنة خوفاً على الناس أن يتشتتوا وتتفرق كلمتهم، فيوجب حدوث ذلك وهنا في الإسلام، ثم تفرغوا بعد ذلك لأمره وأخذوا في تجهيزه ودفنه رضوان الله عليه.
And they ask him to permit them to fight them, but he used to refrain from that due to the meanings that have passed. That was because Hasan, Husayn, and Qanbar – may Allah be pleased with them – attended the house and defended until they were driven out and wounded. And it was not in his view nor in the view of any of the Companions – may Allah be pleased with them – that the matter would reach that extent, but the decreed judgment of Allah was executed and he attained the martyrdom that was written for him. And what they said: that he was left for three days – that is absolutely not correct. How could one think of the Muhajirun and Ansar – may Allah be pleased with them – and especially of Ali (رضي الله عنه) that if a Jew or Christian died near them, they would not be satisfied to leave him as prey for beasts, not covering his private parts nor concealing his nakedness? So how could they permit that regarding Uthman, with his precedence in Islam, his effects in the religion, his connection to the Messenger of Allah by his two daughters, and the Prophet's (peace be upon him) giving him glad tidings of Paradise? This, by Allah, is an open accusation against the Companions in general and against Ali in particular. And if that were proven, the accusation would return upon the one who deemed it permissible for someone like him, not upon him. Unless they were occupied with establishing the imamate and calming the sedition out of fear that the people would scatter and their word would split, thus causing weakness in Islam. Then after that they turned to his affair and undertook his preparation and burial, may Allah be pleased with him.
Source pages p. 1164

Commentary
This passage is both a narrative and a refutation. It first describes the siege: the people asked permission to fight, but Uthman refrained, and Hasan, Husayn, and Qanbar defended until they were forced out. The author then refutes the claim that Uthman's body was left for three days unburied. He argues that this is impossible because the Companions would not even leave a non-Muslim neighbor unburied, let alone a companion of Uthman's stature. He then offers a plausible excuse: the Companions were busy with the urgent matter of establishing the new caliph and calming the fitna, and only afterwards attended to his burial. This refutation defends the honor of the Companions and shows that any delay was due to necessity, not neglect.

Key Terms
المحاربة
الشهادة
الطعن
الفتنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Uthman was left unburied for three days because the Companions did not care about him.
Correction: The author argues that such neglect is unthinkable given the Companions' character, and any delay was due to the pressing need to stabilize the Muslim community after the fitna.

Checkpoint
According to the text, why might the Companions have delayed Uthman's burial?
A) They were busy fighting.
B) They were occupied with establishing the caliphate and calming the sedition.
C) They did not care about him.
D) They were waiting for Ali's return.

Key Takeaway
The author refutes the allegation by appealing to the Companions' noble character and suggests that any delay in burial was due to the urgent need to stabilize the Muslim community.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear negative stories about the Companions, do you instinctively accept them, or do you pause to seek excuses and think well of them? In your daily life, when someone is accused, is your first reaction to believe the worst? Will you resolve to follow the author's example and defend the absent by giving them the benefit of the doubt?
?
The author says the Companions were busy with a crucial matter (the imamate) to prevent the community from scattering, and only then turned to Uthman's burial. Are there urgent responsibilities in your life that cause you to delay other duties, perhaps even duties towards your own family? How can you better balance priorities so that no one feels neglected while you attend to what is most critical?
?
Uthman's virtues are listed to show that he could not possibly have been abandoned. Do you treat people differently based on their status or good deeds? Think of a person you undervalued or neglected. What would it take for you to see their worth and honor them as the author does with Uthman?

Refuting the Poem Attributed to Uthman
Refutes a fabricated poem attributed to Uthman during the siege.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the report of Uthman writing a poem to Ali during the siege is considered baseless according to historical and behavioral evidence.

Core Idea
Uthman's avoidance of war contradicts the plea in the fabricated poem.

In this passage, the author addresses a popular but unsubstantiated report that Caliph Uthman wrote a poem to Ali during the siege. By examining Uthman's well-known character of avoiding conflict and his own words, the author demonstrates the report's lack of foundation. Let's read the argument carefully.

Guided Path
1
Identify the reported poem
Read the line of poetry attributed to Uthman: 'If I am to be eaten, then be the best eater; otherwise, save me before I am torn apart.' Understand that this is a plea for military help.
2
Note the author's immediate dismissal
The author says 'فلا أصل له' (it has no basis). This is a strong claim of fabrication.
3
Examine the evidence from Uthman's character
Uthman was known to avoid war. He even freed slaves who laid down their weapons. This shows his commitment to peace.
He said: 'Whoever lays down his weapon from my slaves is free.'
4
Consider the logical contradiction
If Uthman was avoiding war among his own slaves, how could he ask Ali for military help? The poem contradicts his known behavior.
5
Reflect on the implications
This refutation shows the importance of verifying historical reports against established character and actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما يروون أنه كتب يوم الحصار إلى علي : فإن كنت مأكولاً فكن خير آكل وإلا فأدركني ولما أمزق - فلا أصل له إذ المعروف من أمر عثمان أنه كان يتحامى من الحرب ويتجوز عن ذلك حتى قال: من وضع السلاح من غلماني فهو حر. ومن كان هذا - مع من قصد الحرب من غلمانه - فعله فكيف يستعين بعلي ؟! وكيف يستنصر من هو جاد في نصره مشمر ذيله في ذلك؟! وروى عنه أنه قال : - والله ما قتلت عثمان ولا مالات في قتله - وما روي عن علي أنه قال في أمر عثمان: الله قتله وأنا معه - معناه: وأنا مع عثمان وكانت الهاء عائدة إلى عثمان دون الله تعالى، وأخبر أنه يستشهد كما استشهد عثمان رضي الله عنهما. يحققه أنه قال على المنبر : - قتلت يوم قتل الثور الأبيض - وهو مثل مشهور في العرب، أخبر بذلك أنه يستشهد كما استشهد هو، والله الموفق.
And what they narrate that he wrote during the siege to Ali: 'If I am to be eaten, then be the best eater; otherwise, save me before I am torn apart' – it has no basis. For the known fact about Uthman is that he used to avoid war and resolve to avoid it, to the extent that he said: 'Whoever lays down his weapon from my slaves is free.' And if he did this with those who intended war from his slaves, how could he seek help from Ali?! And how could he seek victory from one who was earnest in his support, rolling up his sleeves for that?! And it is narrated from him that he said: 'By Allah, I did not kill Uthman nor did I incline to his killing.' And what is narrated from Ali that he said regarding the matter of Uthman: 'Allah killed him and I am with him' – its meaning is: I am with Uthman, and the pronoun refers to Uthman, not to Allah Almighty. And he informed that he would be martyred just as Uthman was martyred, may Allah be pleased with them both. This is confirmed by what he said on the pulpit: 'I am killed on the day the white bull is killed' – and this is a well-known proverb among the Arabs. He informed by that that he would be martyred just as he (Uthman) was martyred. And Allah is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 1165

Commentary
This passage refutes two related reports. First, the claim that Uthman wrote a line of poetry to Ali during the siege saying 'If I am to be eaten, then be the best eater.' The author says this has no basis because Uthman was known to avoid war, even freeing slaves who laid down arms, so how could he ask Ali for military help? Second, the report that Ali said 'Allah killed Uthman and I am with him.' The author explains that 'with him' means with Uthman, not with Allah, and that Ali was prophesying his own martyrdom, as confirmed by his statement about the white bull, a proverb meaning he would die a martyr.

Key Terms
التحامي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people believe that the poem is historically authentic and shows Uthman's desperation for help.
Correction: The poem contradicts Uthman's well-documented character of avoiding war, and the author shows it has no basis.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject the poem attributed to Uthman?
A) Because the poem's language is uncharacteristic of Uthman.
B) Because Uthman was known to avoid war and even freed slaves who laid down arms.
C) Because Ali denied receiving any message from Uthman.
D) Because the poem was found in a later source.

Key Takeaway
The poem attributed to Uthman is fabricated because it contradicts his known peaceful character and actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Uthman's consistent character disproved a false narrative. Is there a lie you have believed or spread about someone because you never examined their known character? How will you verify before trusting secondhand reports from now on?
?
Uthman avoided war even when it cost him his life. What principle are you currently compromising for comfort or approval? What would it look like to hold firm at any cost?
?
The author uses clear evidence to refute a claim. When you disagree with someone, do you gather evidence or just dismiss? What step can you take today to base your arguments on facts rather than assumptions?
